<P style="margin-top:8.867px; margin-bottom:0px" align=center><B>NOTES TO AUDITED CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>NOTE 1. </B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:73.333px"><B>DESCRIPTION OF BUSINESS</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The accompanying consolidated financial statements include the accounts of World Waste Technologies, Inc. (Formerly World Waste of America, Inc.) and its wholly owned subsidiaries World Waste of Anaheim, Inc., and World Waste of California, Inc. (collectively the &#147;Company&#148;). All significant inter-company accounts and transactions have been eliminated upon consolidation. World Waste Technologies, Inc. (WWTI), a California corporation, was formed on June&nbsp;18, 2002 as World Waste of America, Inc. WWTI held the United States license from Bio-Products International, Inc. with respect to patented technology developed at the University of Alabama in Huntsville, and other related intellectual property, which technology was designed to convert a significant&nbsp;percent of municipal solid waste into a cellulose biomass containing material. </P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">On March 6, 2009, a majority of the Company&#146;s shareholders voted to merge with a wholly-owned subsidiary of Vertex Energy, Inc. (&#147;Vertex Nevada&#148;). &nbsp;Vertex Nevada, a Nevada corporation based in Houston, Texas, is engaged in the business of recycling used motor oil and other hydrocarbons. Vertex Nevada operates through its Black Oil division, which aggregates used motor oil from third-party collectors and manages the delivery of this feedstock primarily to a third-party re-refining facility, and (2) through its Refining and Marketing division, which aggregates hydrocarbon streams from collectors and generators and manages the delivery of the hydrocarbon waste products to a third-party facility for further processing, and then manages the sale of the end products. In addition, Vertex Nevada proposes to implement proprietary thermo-chemical upgrading technology that will process used motor oil and convert it to higher value pr
oducts such as marine diesel oil and vacuum-gas oil. The accompanying financial statements and footnote disclosures do not reflect the financial impact of the merger, which is expected to close on April 1, 2009. &nbsp;See Note 13.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">In March&nbsp;2004, World Waste of America, Inc. (WWA), merged with a wholly owned subsidiary of Waste Solutions, Inc. (WSI), a California corporation, and changed its name to World Waste Technologies, Inc. (Old WWTI). Cagan McAfee Capital Partners and its affiliates were the controlling shareholders of WSI. Prior to the merger WSI had 7,100,000 shares of common stock outstanding and WWA had 9,100,000 shares of common stock outstanding. The merger was transacted by WSI issuing one of its shares for each share of WWA. After the merger there were 16,200,000 shares outstanding. The transaction was accounted for as a reverse merger of WWA, similar to a recapitalization, because the shareholders of WWA became the controlling shareholders of the entity after the exchange. Accordingly, for accounting purposes, the historical financial statements presented are those of WWA.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">In March&nbsp;2004, Old WWTI entered into an Agreement and Plan of Reorganization with Voice Powered Technologies International, Inc., a California corporation (&#147;VPTI&#148;), to merge with and into VPTI. VPTI was a publicly traded company trading under the stock symbol VPTI.OB. VPTI had no material assets, liabilities or operations. The merger with VPTI was completed on August&nbsp;24, 2004. Pursuant to the merger, Old WWTI shareholders received 20,063,706 VPTI shares or approximately 95% of the outstanding shares of VPTI in exchange for 20,063,706 Old WWTI shares, or a one for one exchange. Upon completion of the merger, VPTI changed its name to World Waste Technologies, Inc. Because the shareholders of Old WWTI became the controlling shareholders of VPTI after the exchange, Old WWTI was treated as the acquirer for accounting purposes, and therefore the transaction was accounted for as a reverse merger. Accordingly, for accounting purpo
ses, the historical financial statements presented are those of Old WWTI.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>NOTE 2. </B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:73.333px"><B>GOING CONCERN</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The accompanying consolidated financial statements have been prepared on a going concern basis, which contemplates the realization of assets and the satisfaction of liabilities in the normal course of business. The Company had a net loss for the year ended December 31, 2008 of $15,205,581 and an accumulated deficit attributable to common shareholders at December 31, 2008 of $85,205,864. The Company expects it will incur substantial additional losses, costs and capital expenditures before it can operate profitably. These issues raise substantial doubt about the Company&#146;s ability to continue as a going concern. The Company is party to a merger agreement with Vertex Energy, Inc. If this transaction fails to close as contemplated, the Company may be unable to continue as a going concern for a reasonable period of time.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px"><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>24</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=center><B>WORLD WASTE TECHNOLOGIES, INC. AND SUBSIDIARIES</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><B>(FORMERLY WORLD WASTE OF AMERICA, INC.)</B></P>

<P style="margin-top:8.867px; margin-bottom:8.867px" align=center><B>NOTES TO AUDITED CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>NOTE 2. </B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:73.333px"><B>GOING CONCERN (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The consolidated financial statements do not include any adjustments relating to the recoverability and classification of recorded asset amounts or the amounts and classification of liabilities that might be necessary should the Company be unable to continue as a going concern. On May&nbsp;15, 2008, the Company entered into a definitive agreement to merge with Vertex Energy, Inc. The agreement was amended and restated on May&nbsp;19, 2008. There can be no assurance that the transaction will be completed. If not closed as contemplated, the Company&#146;s continuation as a going concern remains dependent upon its ability to generate sufficient cash flow to meet its obligations on a timely basis, to obtain additional financing, and ultimately to attain successful operations.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>NOTE 3. </B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:73.333px"><B>SUMMARY OF SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px"><B>Basis of Presentation</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The accompanying consolidated financial statements are prepared in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America. The Company is a new enterprise in the development stage as defined by Statement No.&nbsp;7 of the Financial Accounting Standards Board, since it has not derived substantial revenues from its activities to date.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px"><B>Use of Estimates</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The preparation of consolidated financial statements in conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and the disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the consolidated financial statements and the reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the reporting period. Actual results could differ from those estimates.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px"><B>Revenue Recognition</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">During 2006, revenue for receiving Municipal Solid Waste (MSW) was recognized when the MSW was delivered. Revenue for products sold, such as unbleached fiber, metals and aluminum, are recognized when the product was delivered to the customer.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">All shipping and handling costs were included in gross revenue and accounted for as cost of goods sold.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px"><B>Research and Development</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px">Research and development costs are charged to operations when incurred.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px"><B>Income Taxes</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The Company accounts for income taxes in accordance with Statement of Financial Accounting Standards (&#147;SFAS&#148;) No.&nbsp;109, &#147;Accounting for Income Taxes.&#148; In accordance with SFAS No.&nbsp;109, the Company records a valuation allowance against net deferred tax assets if, based upon the available evidence, it is more likely than not that some or all of the deferred tax assets will not be realized. The ultimate realization of deferred tax assets is dependent upon the generation of future taxable income and when temporary differences become deductible. The Company considers, among other available information, uncertainties surrounding the recoverability of deferred tax assets, scheduled reversals of deferred tax liabilities, projected future taxable income, and other matters in making this assessment.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The Company adopted FIN 48, Accounting for Uncertainty in Income Taxes - An Interpretation of FASB Statement No.&nbsp;109, on January&nbsp;1, 2007. There was no material impact on the Company&#146;s financial statements as a result of the adoption.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>25</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=center><B>WORLD WASTE TECHNOLOGIES, INC. AND SUBSIDIARIES</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><B>(FORMERLY WORLD WASTE OF AMERICA, INC.)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><B>(A DEVELOPMENT STAGE COMPANY)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:8.867px; margin-bottom:8.867px" align=center><B>NOTES TO AUDITED CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>NOTE 3. </B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:73.333px"><B>SUMMARY OF SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px"><B>Cash and Cash Equivalents</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The Company considers all highly liquid investments with a maturity of three months or less when purchased, which are not securing any corporate obligations, to be cash equivalents.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px"><B>Short Term Investments</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The Company determines the appropriate classification of its investments at the time of acquisition and reevaluates such determination at each balance sheet date. During the the third quarter 2008, all short term investments held for sale, which included auction rate securities, were sold and the proceeds are included in cash and cash equivalents. The Company recognized a loss of approximately $389,000, recorded in Other Income and (Expense), upon the sale. &nbsp;All investments held at December&nbsp;31, 2007 were short-term available for sale securities, and were carried at quoted fair value, with unrealized gains and losses reported in shareholders&#146; equity as a component of accumulated comprehensive income. </P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px"><B>Concentration of Credit Risk</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">The Company maintains its cash balances at financial institutions. Cash balances at the institutions are insured by the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation up to $250,000. All cash equivalents are invested in government securities.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px"><B>Fixed Assets</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">The Company reviews fixed assets for impairment whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that their carrying amount may not be recoverable. If the review indicates that fixed assets are not recoverable (i.e. the carrying amounts are more than the future projected undiscounted cash flows), their carrying amounts would be reduced to fair value.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">During 2008, all remaining fixed assets were liquidated. Machinery and equipment was stated at cost. Prior to the fixed assets being recorded as held for sale, depreciation was computed on the straight-line method over the estimated useful asset lives or for leasehold improvements or equipment installed in our Anaheim plant (no longer leased or otherwise being used by us), over the remaining life of the lease, whichever was shorter. Due to the fact that at the time the assets were placed into service the lease had 8 years and two months remaining, all assets and leasehold improvements at the Anaheim facility were being depreciated over a maximum of 8 years and two months on a straight line basis. Maintenance and repairs are expensed as incurred.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The Company completed the construction of its initial plant in Anaheim, California early in the second quarter of 2006. The Company placed into service and began depreciating the assets related to this facility in the second quarter of 2006.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The assets at the Anaheim plant were comprised of two basic technologies; the front half of the plant consisted of assets related to the Company&#146;s patented technology related to &#147;steam classification&#148; and material separation and the back half of the plant consist of assets related to screening and cleaning of the cellulose biomass material to prepare it for sale to paper mills. During the plant start up phase, we confronted several issues, including an unexpected high level of biological oxygen demand from organic waste in the wastewater from the pulp screening and cleaning process. The Company decided not to make the capital improvements necessary to the Anaheim plant&#146;s wetlap process, or &#147;back half&#148; which the Company considered necessary in order to recover the carrying amount of the wetlap plant assets through projected future undiscounted cash flow from its operation. Consequently, the Company recorded a char
ge of $9,737,344 in 2006 which represented the net carrying value of the wetlap process (or &#147;back half&#148;) equipment.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>26</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=center><B>WORLD WASTE TECHNOLOGIES, INC. AND SUBSIDIARIES</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><B>(FORMERLY WORLD WASTE OF AMERICA, INC.)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><B>(A DEVELOPMENT STAGE COMPANY)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:8.867px; margin-bottom:8.867px" align=center><B>NOTES TO AUDITED CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>NOTE 3. </B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:73.333px"><B>SUMMARY OF SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px"><B>Fixed Assets (Continued)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The Company did not record an impairment charge for the steam classification equipment (or &#147;front half&#148;) of the plant at that time because the Company intended to use that equipment in research and development activities as part of its development of alternative back end processes such as, but not limited to, gasification and acid hydrolysis.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">During the third quarter of 2007, the Company determined that the ongoing research and development work would more efficiently be carried out at the location of Applied Power Concepts, the Company&#146;s research and development partner. Consequently, in order to reduce costs and focus management attention and cash resources on the Company&#146;s renewable energy process, the Company initiated conversations with Taormina regarding termination of the lease of the Anaheim Facility and the cancellation of the associated recycling agreement. On October&nbsp;29, 2007, Taormina terminated the lease and the recycling agreement, effective as of October&nbsp;31, 2007. Consequently, the Company recorded a charge of $8,454,106 in the third quarter of 2007 which represents the net carrying value of the assets at the Anaheim plant, net of estimated fair value of the equipment and estimated costs of the equipment removal and scrap. The estimated net carryi
ng value was reevaluated at December&nbsp;31, 2007. As of December 31, 2008, the Company had sold or disposed of all the equipment.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">The Company capitalizes leases in accordance with FASB 13, &#147;Accounting for Leases.&#148;</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px"><B>Intangibles</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">Intangible assets are recorded at cost.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">The Company&#146;s policy regarding intangible assets is to review such intangible assets for impairment whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that their carrying amount may not be recoverable. If the review indicates that intangible assets are not recoverable (i.e. the carrying amounts are more than the future projected undiscounted cash flows), their carrying amounts would be reduced to fair value. </P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px"><B>Redeemable Convertible Preferred Stock</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">Convertible Preferred Stock which may be redeemable for cash at the determination of the holder is classified as mezzanine equity, in accordance with FAS 150 &#147;Accounting for Certain Financial Instruments with Characteristics of Both Debt and Equity,&#148; EITF Topic D 98 and ASR 268, and is shown net of discounts for offering costs, warrant values and beneficial conversion features.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px"><B>Stock-Based Compensation</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">As of December&nbsp;31, 2008, the Company had two share-based compensation plans, which are described below. The compensation cost that has been charged against income for the plans was $1,638,319 and $1,638,128 for the years ended, December&nbsp;31, 2008 and December&nbsp;31, 2007, respectively. Because the Company is in a net loss position, no income tax benefit has been recognized in the income statement for share-based compensation arrangements. As of December&nbsp;31, 2008, no share-based compensation cost had been capitalized as part of inventory or fixed assets.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">The Company&#146;s 2004 Incentive Stock Option Plan (the 2004 Plan), which is shareholder-approved, provides for the issuance by the Company of a total of up to 2.0&nbsp;million shares of common stock and options to acquire common stock to the Company&#146;s employees, directors and consultants. The Company granted options to acquire no shares under this Plan during the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2008 to employees, members of the board of directors and consultants. At December&nbsp;31, 2008, there were 1,696,167 options outstanding under the Plan.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">In May&nbsp;of 2007 the board of directors approved the Company&#146;s 2007 Incentive Stock Plan (the 2007 Plan), which is not shareholder-approved. The 2007 Plan provides for the issuance by the Company of a total of up to 6.0&nbsp;million shares of common stock and options to acquire common stock to the Company&#146;s employees, directors and consultants in 2008. The Company formed a Special Committee of its Board of Directors, comprised of four </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>27</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:73.333px"><B>SUMMARY OF SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px"><B>Stock-Based Compensation (Continued)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px">directors, to evaluate the Company&#146;s strategic alternatives, and the Special Committee retained a financial advisor to assist in this process. These alternatives included, but were not limited to, a sale or merger of the Company and/or a restructuring. &nbsp;As compensation for serving on the Special Committee, each of the members thereof is entitled to receive a monthly payment of $5,000 for the period the Special Committee continues to function, and was granted an option to acquire up to 300,000, or a total of 1,200,000, shares of common stock pursuant to the Company&#146;s 2007 Plan. Each option has an exercise price equal to $0.155 per share (the closing price of the Company&#146;s common stock on the date of grant) and vested in six equal monthly installments commencing as of March&nbsp;27, 2008. </P>
<P style="margin:0px; text-indent:48px">The Company granted options to acquire a total of 1,575,000 shares during the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2008 to employees, members of the board of directors and consultants. At December&nbsp;31, 2008, there were 4,292,120 options outstanding under the Plan.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The Company believes that option awards better align the interests of its employees with those of its shareholders. Option awards are generally granted with an exercise price equal to the market price of the Company&#146;s stock at the date of grant; those option awards generally vest based on 2 to 4 years of continuous service and have 10-year contractual terms. Certain option awards provide for accelerated vesting if there is a change in control (as defined in each Plan).</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The fair value of each option award is estimated on the date of grant using the Black-Scholes option valuation model that uses the assumptions noted in the table below. Expected volatilities are based on the historical volatility of the Company&#146;s common stock from August&nbsp;24, 2004 through the date of the respective grant. The Company uses historical data to estimate option exercise and employee terminations within the valuation model. The expected term of options granted was estimated using the simple method which the Company believes provides a reasonable estimation of the period of time that options granted are expected to be outstanding. The risk-free rate for periods within the contractual life of the option is based on the LIBOR rate at the time of grant.</P>

<P style="margin-top:8.867px; margin-bottom:8.867px"><B>Earnings per Share</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The Company has adopted Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;128, &#147;Earnings per Share&#148; (SFAS No.&nbsp;128). SFAS No.&nbsp;128 provides for the calculation of basic and diluted earnings per share.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">Basic earnings per share includes no dilution and is computed by dividing income available to common shareholders by the weighted average number of common shares outstanding for the period. Diluted earnings per share reflects the potential dilution of securities that could share in the earnings of an entity, such as stock options, warrants or convertible securities. Due to their anti-dilutive effect, common stock equivalents of 30,851,374, consisting of employee options of 5,988,000, non employment warrants of 6,829,828, Preferred Series&nbsp;A of 6,505,978 and Preferred Series&nbsp;B of 11,527,568, were not included in the calculation of diluted earnings per share at December&nbsp;31, 2008. Common stock equivalents of 28,337,007, consisting of employee options of 4,843,000, non employment warrants of 6,829,827, Preferred Series&nbsp;A of 6,010,516 and Preferred Series&nbsp;B of 10,653,664, were not included in the calculation of diluted earn
ings per share at December&nbsp;31, 2007. </P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px"><B>New Accounting Pronouncements</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:8.867px; margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:48px">FASB issued Statement of Financial Accounting Standards (&#147;SFAS&#148;) No.&nbsp;157, &#147;Fair Value Measurements&#148;. This new standard provides guidance for using fair value to measure assets and liabilities and information about the extent to which companies measure assets and liabilities at fair value, the information used to measure fair value, and the effect of fair value measurements on earnings. This framework is intended to provide increased consistency in how fair value determinations are made under various existing accounting standards which permit, or in some cases require, estimates of fair market value. SFAS 157 also expands financial statement disclosure requirements about a company&#146;s use of fair value measurements, including the effect of such measures on earnings. The provisions of SFAS No.&nbsp;157 are effective for fiscal years beginning after November&nbsp;15, 2007. Adoption of this pronouncement did not have a
 material impact on the Company&#146;s consolidated financial statements.</P>

<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=center><B>WORLD WASTE TECHNOLOGIES, INC. AND SUBSIDIARIES</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><B>(FORMERLY WORLD WASTE OF AMERICA, INC.)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><B>(A DEVELOPMENT STAGE COMPANY)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:8.867px; margin-bottom:8.867px" align=center><B>NOTES TO AUDITED CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>NOTE 3. </B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:73.333px"><B>SUMMARY OF SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px"><B>New Accounting Pronouncements (Continued)</B></P>
<P style="line-height:11pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">The FASB issued SFAS No.&nbsp;159, The Fair Value Option for Financial Assets and Financial Liabilities-Including an Amendment of FASB Statement No.&nbsp;115(SFAS No.&nbsp;159). This standard permits an entity to choose to measure many financial instruments and certain other items at fair value. The accounting provisions of SFAS No.&nbsp;159 are effective for financial statements issued for fiscal years beginning after November&nbsp;15, 2007. Adoption of this pronouncement did not have a material impact on the Company&#146;s consolidated financial statements. </P>
<P style="line-height:11pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">On December&nbsp;4, 2007, the FASB issued FASB Statement No.&nbsp;141 (Revised 2007). Under Statement 141R, an acquiring entity will be required to recognize all the assets acquired and liabilities assumed in a transaction at the acquisition-date fair value with limited exceptions. Statement 141R will change the accounting treatment for certain specific items, including: acquisition costs will be generally expensed as incurred; noncontrolling interests (formerly known as &#147;minority interests&#148; -- see Statement 160 discussion below) will be valued at fair value at the acquisition date; acquired contingent liabilities will be recorded at fair value at the acquisition date and subsequently measured at either the higher of such amount or the amount determined under existing guidance for non-acquired contingencies; in-process research and development will be recorded at fair value as an indefinite-lived intangible asset a
t the acquisition date; restructuring costs associated with a business combination will be generally expensed subsequent to the acquisition date; and changes in deferred tax asset valuation allowances and income tax uncertainties after the acquisition date generally will affect income tax expense. Statement 141R also includes a substantial number of new disclosure requirements. Statement 141R applies prospectively to business combinations for which the acquisition date is on or after the beginning of the first annual reporting period beginning on or after December&nbsp;15, 2008. The Company does not expect the adoption No. 141R to have a material impact on its consolidated financial statements.</P>
<P style="line-height:11pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">SFAS No.&nbsp;160, Noncontrolling Interests in Consolidated Financial Statements - An Amendment of ARB No.&nbsp;51. On December&nbsp;4, 2007, the FASB issued FASB Statement No.&nbsp;160. Statement 160 establishes new accounting and reporting standards for the noncontrolling interest in a subsidiary and for the deconsolidation of a subsidiary. Specifically, this statement requires the recognition of a noncontrolling interest (minority interest) as equity in the consolidated financial statements and separate from the parent&#146;s equity. The amount of net income attributable to the noncontrolling interest will be included in consolidated net income on the face of the income statement. Statement 160 clarifies that changes in a parent&#146;s ownership interest in a subsidiary that do not result in deconsolidation are equity transactions if the parent retains its controlling financial interest. In addition, this statement requir
es that a parent recognize a gain or loss in net income when a subsidiary is deconsolidated. Such gain or loss will be measured using the fair value of the noncontrolling equity investment on the deconsolidation date. Statement 160 also includes expanded disclosure requirements regarding the interests of the parent and its noncontrolling interest. Statement 160 is effective for fiscal years, and interim periods within those fiscal years, beginning on or after December&nbsp;15, 2008. Because the Company has no such arrangements currently, the adoption of this principle will not have a material impact on the Company&#146;s financial statements. However, as the Company pursues its gasification strategy, it may have such arrangements in the future.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>NOTE 4. </B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:73.333px"><B>PATENT AND LICENSE AGREEMENT</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">On June&nbsp;21, 2002, the Company entered into a U.S. technology sub-license agreement with Bio-Products International, Inc. (BPI), an Alabama corporation with respect to certain intellectual property and patented methods and processes. This agreement was amended on June&nbsp;21, 2004 and again on August&nbsp;19, 2006. The technology was designed to provide for the processing and separation of material contained in Municipal Solid Waste (MSW). Through April&nbsp;30, 2006, the University of Alabama in Huntsville (&#147;UAH&#148;) owned the patent for this technology. On May&nbsp;1, 2006, the Company acquired the patent from UAH for $100,000 and 167,000 shares of the Company&#146;s unregistered common stock valued at its fair value on the date of issuance of approximately $698,000. The patent reverts to UAH in the event of bankruptcy of the Company. This patent is licensed to BPI. The license to the patent in the United States was assigned to 
the Company.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>30</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=center><B>WORLD WASTE TECHNOLOGIES, INC. AND SUBSIDIARIES</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><B>(FORMERLY WORLD WASTE OF AMERICA, INC.)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:7.8px" align=center><B>(A DEVELOPMENT STAGE COMPANY)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:7.8px" align=center><B>NOTES TO AUDITED CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px"><B>NOTE 4. </B></P>
<P style="line-height:11pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:7.8px; text-indent:73.333px"><B>PATENT AND LICENSE AGREEMENT (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="line-height:11pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:7.8px; text-indent:48px">In April&nbsp;2007, the Company filed a lawsuit against BPI alleging, among other things, breach of contract and negligence with respect to the construction of the vessels.</P>
<P style="line-height:11pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:7.8px; text-indent:48px">During the fourth quarter of 2007, the Company determined it would not use the technologies related to the intangible assets in its future plants. Consequently, it reclassified the unamortized intangible assets to Assets Held for Sale and accounted for at the lower of fair value less cost to sell (net fair value) or carrying value. In March&nbsp;of 2008, the Company entered into a definitive agreement to sell the intangible Assets, settle the lawsuit with BPI and sell a significant amount of the assets which were used in the Anaheim plant to exploit the patent for a total of approximately $1.9&nbsp;million. Because the carrying value is less than the net fair value no adjustment was recorded.</P>
<P style="line-height:11pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:7.8px; text-indent:48px">In March&nbsp;2008, the Company entered into an agreement with Clean Earth Solutions, Inc. (&#147;CES&#148;), pursuant to which it agreed (i) to sell to CES specified assets relating to the &#147;front end&#148; process of World Waste&#146;s Anaheim Facility for a cash payment to the Company of $500,000 (the &#147;First Closing&#148;), (ii) to settle a dispute arising from design issues related to the steam classification vessels that the Company had intended to use in its operations, in exchange for a payment to us of $640,000 (the &#147;Second Closing&#148;) and (iii) to sell to CES all of the Company&#146;s intellectual property rights in its pressurized steam classification process in exchange for a payment of $800,000 (of which $236,000 was previously paid by CES) (the &#147;Third Closing&#148;). On March&nbsp;7, 2008, CES paid $500,000, and the First Closing was consummated. In June&nbsp;2008, CES paid the Company $640,0
00 for the Second Closing. Pursuant to this agreement, the Third Closing was to occur on such a date as determined by CES, provided that the Third Closing could not occur later than July&nbsp;31, 2008.</P>
<P style="line-height:11pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:7.8px; text-indent:48px">As a result of the default by CES, the Third Closing never occurred. On October&nbsp;22, 2008, the Company sold the patent and related intellectual property rights in its pressurized steam classification process to CleanTech Biofuels, Inc. (&#147;CTB&#148;) in exchange for $150,000 in cash, a $450,000 secured promissory note and warrants to purchase up to 900,000 shares of CTB&#146;s common stock. The promissory note matures on July&nbsp;22, 2009, bears interest at 6.0% per annum and is secured by the patent. The warrants are exercisable at any time for five years from the date of issuance at a price of $0.45 per share. In addition, CTB issued the Company a contingent warrant to purchase up to an additional 900,000 shares of its common stock on the same terms, except that this warrant is exercisable only if CTB defaults on its obligations under the note. &nbsp;Due to the uncertainty of the collectability of the note, the Compa
ny had fully reserved the balance of $450,000 as of December 31, 2008, and is therefore not included in the Company&#146;s consolidated financial statements. &nbsp;The warrants were valued in accordance with SFAS No. 157, utilizing the Black Scholes model. &nbsp;Using the five year treasury bill risk free interest rate of 2.56%, historical volatility of 203%, the contractual exercise price of $0.45 per warrant, and a fair value per warrant of $0.03, the total value of the warrant grnat was immaterial to the Company&#146;s financial statements. The contingent warrant was not valued or reflected in the Company&#146;s financial statements as their issuance is contingent on an event (default of the note) that has not occurred.</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px"><B>NOTE 5. </B></P>
<P style="line-height:11pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:7.8px; text-indent:73.333px"><B>TERMINATION OF SIGNIFICANT CONTRACT</B></P>
<P style="line-height:11pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:7.8px; text-indent:48px">In June&nbsp;2003 the Company entered into a multi-year recycle agreement with Taormina Industries, Inc. pursuant to which, among other things, Taormina agreed to deliver residual municipal solid waste (MSW) to the Company for processing and the Company agreed to lease a building for the related recycling facility on Taormina&#146;s campus in Anaheim, California (the &#147;Anaheim Facility&#148;). The lease for the Anaheim Facility was entered into in July&nbsp;2004. The recycling agreement, as amended, provided that the recycling agreement would terminate automatically upon termination of the lease.</P>
<P style="line-height:11pt; margin:0px; text-indent:48px">As previously disclosed, during early 2007 the Company began using the Anaheim Facility to conduct research and development activities related to the production of renewable energy from MSW. Recently the Company determined that the ongoing research and development work would more efficiently be carried out at the location of Applied Power Concepts, the Company&#146;s research and development partner. Consequently, in order to reduce costs and focus management attention and cash resources on the Company&#146;s renewable energy process, the Company initiated conversations with Taormina regarding termination of the lease of the Anaheim Facility and the cancellation of the associated recycling agreement. On October&nbsp;29, 2007, Taormina terminated the lease and the recycling agreement, effective as of October&nbsp;31, 2007. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR>

<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px"><B>NOTE 5. </B></P>
<P style="line-height:11pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:7.8px; text-indent:73.333px"><B>TERMINATION OF SIGNIFICANT CONTRACT (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">On November&nbsp;7, 2007, Taormina filed an unlawful detainer action in the Superior Court of the State of California, County of Orange (the &#147;Action&#148;) against the Company as to the Anaheim Facility. On March&nbsp;5, 2008, Taormina and the Company entered into a stipulation for entry of judgment in the Action (the &#147;Stipulation&#148;). The Stipulation provides for: (a) the cancellation and forfeiture of the lease; (b) the Company to make a payment of $192,218 (the &#147;Payment&#148;) to Taormina; and (c) the Company to remain in possession of the Anaheim Facility until June&nbsp;30, 2008. As of December 31, 2008, the Company had &nbsp;made the Payment to Taormina and had completed its orderly exit from the facility.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The non-competition and right of first refusal provisions of the recycle agreement will survive termination of such agreement through July&nbsp;25, 2014 (the date that the lease would have expired had it not been terminated).</P>

<P style="margin-top:8.867px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The Company has recorded a valuation allowance in the amount set forth above for certain deferred tax assets where it is more likely than not the Company will not realize future tax benefits related to these items. The net changes in the valuation allowance for the fiscal years ended December&nbsp;31, 2008 and 2007, and for the period from June&nbsp;18, 2002 (Inception) through December&nbsp;31, 2008 were $1,441,369, $6,172,540, and $118,552,662, respectively.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">As of December&nbsp;31, 2008, the Company has federal and state net operating loss carryforwards available to offset future taxable income of approximately $43,304,661 and $41,191,113, respectively. These federal and state net operating loss carryforwards expire through 2027 and 2017, respectively.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The Tax Reform Act of 1986 imposed substantial restrictions on the utilization of NOLs in the event of an &#147;ownership change&#148; (as defined in the Internal Revenue Code) of a corporation. The NOLs attributable to Voice Powered Technology International before its merger with World Waste of America, Inc. are almost completely limited according to these provisions. As such, the Company has excluded a significant portion of them in this analysis.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">On January 1, 2007 the Company adopted the provisions of FASB Interpretation No. 48, Accounting for Uncertainty in Income Taxes - an interpretation of FASB Statement No. 109 (&quot;FIN 48&quot;). FIN 48 prescribes a recognition threshold and measurement attribute for the financial statement recognition and measurement of a tax position taken or expected to be taken in a tax return. FIN 48 requires that a Company determine whether the benefits of tax positions are more likely than not of being sustained upon audit based on the technical merits of the tax position. For tax positions that are more likely than not of being sustained upon audit, the Company recognizes the largest amount of the benefits that are more likely than not of being sustained in the financial statements. For tax positions that are not more likely than not of being sustained upon audit, the Company does not recognize any portion of the benefit in the financial statements. <
/P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The adoption of FIN 48 did not have a material effect on the financial statements and therefore no portion of the Company's net deferred tax asset (before being fully reserved) has been adjusted by the application of FIN 48. </P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">We have historically classified interest and penalties on income tax liabilities as additional income tax expense and expect to continue to do so after the adoption of FIN 48. As of December 31, 2008, our statement of financial position included no accrued interest or penalties.</P>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The Company and its subsidiaries file income tax returns in the U.S. and various state and local jurisdictions. As of December 31, 2008, the Company was not under examination by any major tax Jurisdiction. The tax years that remain subject to examination by significant jurisdiction are as follows:</P>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">California: 2004 through the current period.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>NOTE 7. </B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:73.333px"><B>REDEEMABLE CONVERTIBLE PREFERRED STOCK</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px"><B>8% Series A Cumulative Redeemable Convertible Participating Preferred Stock</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">On April&nbsp;28, 2005, the Company issued and sold 4,000,000 shares of its newly created 8% Series&nbsp;A Cumulative Redeemable Convertible Participating Preferred Stock (the &#147;Series&nbsp;A&#148;) and warrants (the &#147;Warrants,&#148; and, together with the Series&nbsp;A Preferred, the &#147;Securities&#148;) to purchase up to 400,000 shares of common stock of the Company. On May&nbsp;9, 2005, the Company entered into a Securities Purchase Agreement whereby the Company issued and sold an additional 75,600 shares of Series&nbsp;A Preferred and Warrants to purchase up to 7,560 shares of common stock of the Company. The gross aggregate proceeds to the Company from the sale of the Securities was $10,189,000.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The certificate of determination governing the terms of the Series&nbsp;A provides for the Series&nbsp;A to convert into shares of common stock at a conversion rate of one-for-one. In February&nbsp;2006, however, the Company contractually agreed with the holders of the Series&nbsp;A to provide for an increase in this conversion rate upon subsequent issuances of shares of common stock (subject to specified exceptions) at a price less than 115% of the conversion rate in effect at the time of issuance. As a result of this agreement, on May&nbsp;25, 2006 (the date the Company first issued shares of its Series&nbsp;B Preferred, as described below), the conversion rate was adjusted to approximately 1.18 shares of common stock for each one share of Series&nbsp;A.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The Company was required to apply the proceeds of the sale of the Securities primarily to the construction and operation of the Company&#146;s initial plant in Anaheim, California. The holders of the Series&nbsp;A currently have the right to elect a majority of the members of the Company&#146;s Board of Directors. This right will terminate, however, upon the first to occur of the Operational Date (generally defined as if and when the Company generates total operating cash flow of at least $672,000 for any consecutive three month period or the date on which less than 50% of the shares of Series&nbsp;A remain outstanding).</P>
<P style="margin-top:8.867px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">Holders of Series&nbsp;A are entitled to receive cumulative dividends, payable quarterly in additional shares of Series&nbsp;A, at the rate of 8% per annum. This dividend rate was increased to 9% as of January&nbsp;28, 2006 pursuant to the terms of the Series&nbsp;A as a result of the Company&#146;s failure to comply with certain registration rights provisions. As of December&nbsp;5, 2006, the registration statement was declared effective and the dividend rate reverted to 8%.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">Each share of Series&nbsp;A is entitled to that number of votes equal to the number of whole shares of Common Stock into which it is convertible. In addition, so long as at least 50% of the shares of Series&nbsp;A remain outstanding, the Company is prohibited from taking certain actions without the approval of the holders of a majority of the outstanding shares of Series&nbsp;A.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The holders of a majority of the shares of Series&nbsp;A have the option to require the Company to redeem all outstanding shares of Series&nbsp;A on April&nbsp;28, 2010 at a redemption price equal to $2.50 per share, plus accrued and unpaid dividends to that date. Assuming no conversion of shares of Series&nbsp;A, this amount will be equal to approximately $15&nbsp;million. In the event the holders do not exercise this redemption right, all shares of Series&nbsp;A will automatically convert into shares of Common Stock on such date, as described below.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center>34</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=center><B>WORLD WASTE TECHNOLOGIES, INC. AND SUBSIDIARIES</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><B>(FORMERLY WORLD WASTE OF AMERICA, INC.)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:7.8px" align=center><B>(A DEVELOPMENT STAGE COMPANY)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:7.8px" align=center><B>NOTES TO AUDITED CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px"><B>NOTE 7. </B></P>
<P style="line-height:11pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:7.8px; text-indent:73.333px"><B>REDEEMABLE CONVERTIBLE PREFERRED STOCK (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">Because the Series&nbsp;A is redeemable at the end of five years, at the option of the holder, it has been classified as &#147;mezzanine equity&#148; on the balance sheet, in accordance with FAS 150, EITF Topic D 98 and ASR 268.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">Each share of Series&nbsp;A will automatically convert into shares of Common Stock at the stated conversion rate (i) in the event the Company consummates an underwritten public offering of its securities at a price per share not less than $5.00 and for a total gross offering amount of at least $10&nbsp;million, (ii) in the event of a sale of the Company resulting in proceeds to the holders of Series&nbsp;A of a per share amount of at least $5.00, (iii) in the event that the closing market price of the Common Stock averages at least $7.50 per share over a period of 20 consecutive trading days and the daily trading volume averages at least 75,000 shares over such period, (iv) upon the approval of a majority of the then-outstanding shares of Series&nbsp;A, or (v) unless the Company is otherwise obligated to redeem the shares as described above, on April&nbsp;28, 2010.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">Each holder has the right to convert its shares of Series&nbsp;A into shares of Common Stock at the stated conversion rate at any time (subject to certain contractual restrictions in the event such conversion would result in the holder being the beneficial holder of more than 4.99% of the Company&#146;s outstanding shares of common stock).</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The Warrants are exercisable for a period of five years commencing as of their issuance date, initially at an exercise price of $4.00 per share (which exercise price was subsequently revised as described in subheading SERIES A CONSENTS). The fair value of the Warrants was $1,328,066 on the issuance date. The value of the Warrants was estimated using the Black-Scholes option pricing model with the following assumptions: average risk-free interest of 6.75%; dividend yield of 0%; average volatility factor of the expected market price of the Company&#146;s common stock of 70%; and a term of 5 years. The value of the Warrants was deducted from the face amount of the Series&nbsp;A Preferred and is being amortized as dividends. In accordance with EITF 00-19, the value of the Warrants has been recorded as a liability until such time as the Company meets the registration obligation of the underlying shares. In accordance with SFAS 133, the warrant lia
bility is adjusted at the end of each reporting period to its fair value, and the adjustment is classified as other income (expense). The Company recognized $1,079,721 and $709,412 of other income for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2006 and 2005, respectively. The Company met the registration obligation on December&nbsp;5, 2006 and the warrant liability was eliminated through additional paid in capital. The Company has determined no liability is necessary to be recognized in accordance with SFAS 5.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">In accordance with EITF 98-5 and 00-27 it was determined that the Series&nbsp;A&#146;s effective conversion price was issued at a discount to fair value. The value of this discount, called a beneficial conversion feature, was determined to be $1,328,066. The beneficial conversion feature was deducted from the carrying value of the Series&nbsp;A and is being amortized over five years. The amortization amount is treated consistent with the treatment of preferred stock dividends.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">In connection with the issuance of the Securities, on April&nbsp;28, 2005, the Company entered into a registration rights agreement granting the holders certain demand and piggyback registration rights with respect of the common stock issuable upon conversion of the Series&nbsp;A and exercise of the Warrants. The Company filed a registration statement with the SEC on August&nbsp;4, 2005 to register these shares for resale. This registration statement was withdrawn on December&nbsp;19, 2005. In May&nbsp;of 2006, the Company entered into an amended and restated registration rights agreement granting the Series&nbsp;A holders all the same rights received by the Series&nbsp;B holders. A new registration statement covering the resale of these shares has been filed. The registration statement was declared effective December&nbsp;5, 2006. The registration rights agreement stipulated that if the registration statement was not declared effective by No
vember&nbsp;21, 2006, the Company had to pay 1&nbsp;percent per month for a maximum of 6 months or 6&nbsp;percent maximum. Between November&nbsp;21, 2006 and December&nbsp;4, 2006, the Company became obligated to pay the Series&nbsp;A Preferred Shareholders $50,000 in liquidated damages in the form of additional shares of Series&nbsp;A Preferred Stock. In connection with this transaction, certain of the Company&#146;s officers and significant shareholders (the &#147;Locked Up Holders&#148;), beneficially owning approximately 13&nbsp;million shares of Common Stock, agreed that, subject to certain exceptions, they would not offer, sell, contract to sell, lend, pledge, grant any option to purchase, make any short sale or otherwise dispose of any shares of Common Stock, or any options or warrants to purchase </P>

<P style="margin-top:8.867px; margin-bottom:8.867px"><B>Series A Consents</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The consent of the holders of the Series&nbsp;A was required in order to consummate the issuance of the Senior Secured Debt. On February&nbsp;6, 2006, the holders of the Series&nbsp;A gave such consent pursuant to a letter agreement with the Company (the &#147;Series&nbsp;A Agreement&#148;). Pursuant to the Series&nbsp;A Agreement, among other things, (i) the Company agreed to call a shareholders meeting to approve an amendment of certain provisions of the certificate of determination governing the terms of the Series&nbsp;A (including the change to the conversion rate described above), and (ii) the holders of Series&nbsp;A agreed to waive certain of their veto rights and contractual rights, in order to facilitate the Company&#146;s next round of financing. In consideration of the foregoing, the Company agreed to deliver to the holders of Series&nbsp;A additional warrants (&#147;Additional Warrants&#148;)to purchase up to a total of 407,560 s
hares of the Company&#146;s Common Stock at an exercise price of $0.01 per share. The Additional Warrants are exercisable for a period of five years commencing as of their issuance date. The fair value of the warrants, $1,647,250, was expensed during the quarter ended March&nbsp;31, 2006 as financing expense. The value of the warrants was estimated using the Black-Scholes option pricing model with the following assumptions: average risk-free interest of 4.82%; dividend yield of 0%; average volatility factor of the expected market price of the Company&#146;s common stock of 70%; and a term of five years.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">On April&nbsp;12, 2006, in connection with obtaining the consent of the holders of the Series&nbsp;A to the issuance of shares of the Company&#146;s Series&nbsp;B Preferred Stock described below, the Company agreed to increase the number of shares issuable upon exercise of the original Warrants from 407,560 shares to 1,018,900 shares (&#147;New Warrants&#148;), and to decrease the exercise price from $4.00 per share to $2.75 per share. The change in the estimated value calculated using the Black-Scholes option pricing model between the original Warrants and the New Warrants of $1,135,487 was charged to other expense during the second quarter of 2006. The value of the warrants was calculated with the following assumptions: average risk-free interest of 5.42%; dividend yield of 0%; average volatility factor of the expected market price of the Company&#146;s common stock of 70%; and a term of 3 years.</P>

<P style="margin:0px" align=center>36</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=center><B>WORLD WASTE TECHNOLOGIES, INC. AND SUBSIDIARIES</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><B>(FORMERLY WORLD WASTE OF AMERICA, INC.)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:7.8px" align=center><B>(A DEVELOPMENT STAGE COMPANY)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:7.8px" align=center><B>NOTES TO AUDITED CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px"><B>NOTE 7. </B></P>
<P style="line-height:11pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:7.8px; text-indent:73.333px"><B>REDEEMABLE CONVERTIBLE PREFERRED STOCK (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">In addition, the conversion price of the Series&nbsp;A was decreased. Following the guidance of FAS 123R, paragraph 35 for modification to equity instruments, the incremental value of the modification, computed as the difference between the fair value of the conversion feature at the new conversion price and conversion feature at the old conversion price on the modification date was deducted from earnings available to common stockholders as an effective dividend to preferred shareholders, following the presentation guidance in EITF Topic D-42. The change in the estimated value of the conversion feature using the Black-Scholes option pricing model between the original conversion price to the new conversion price was $3,065,931. The values of the conversion features were calculated with the following assumptions: average risk-free interest of 4.97%; dividend yield of 0%; average volatility factor of the expected market price of the Company&#146
;s common stock of 70% and a term of 3 years.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px"><B>8% Series B Cumulative Redeemable Convertible Participating Preferred Stock</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">On May&nbsp;25 and May&nbsp;30, 2006, the Company issued and sold a total of 284,888 shares of its newly created 8% Series&nbsp;B Cumulative Redeemable Convertible Participating Preferred Stock (the &#147;Series&nbsp;B&#148;) and common stock purchase warrants. A portion of these securities were sold for $25,000,000 in cash and a portion were issued in exchange for the cancellation of $3,488,800 aggregate principal amount of Senior Debt (including accrued interest). Each share of Series&nbsp;B converts into 40 shares of common stock (subject to anti-dilution adjustments). The shares of Series&nbsp;B are convertible into a total of 11,395,520 shares of Common Stock and the warrants provide the holders with the right to purchase up to a total of 2,848,880 additional shares of common stock of the Company.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">Each share of Series&nbsp;B is entitled to that number of votes equal to the number of whole shares of the Common Stock into which it is convertible. In addition, so long as at least 50% of the shares of Series&nbsp;B remain outstanding, the Company is prohibited from taking certain actions without the approval of the holders of a majority of the outstanding shares of Series&nbsp;B.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">The holders of a majority of the shares of Series&nbsp;B have the option to require the Company to redeem all outstanding shares of Series&nbsp;B on April&nbsp;28, 2010 at a redemption price equal to $100 per share, plus accrued and unpaid dividends to that date. Assuming no further shares of Series&nbsp;B are converted, this amount will be approximately $32&nbsp;million. In the event the holders do not exercise this redemption right, all shares of Series&nbsp;B will automatically convert into shares of Common Stock on such date, as described below.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">Because the Series&nbsp;B is redeemable at the end of four years, at the option of the holder, it has been classified as &#147;mezzanine equity&#148; on the balance sheet, in accordance with FAS 150, EITF Topic D 98 and ASR 268.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">Each share of Series&nbsp;B will automatically convert into shares of Common Stock at the stated conversion rate (i) in the event the Company consummates an underwritten public offering of its securities at a price per share not less than $5.00 and for a total gross offering amount of at least $20&nbsp;million, (ii) in the event of a sale of the Company resulting in proceeds to the holders of Series&nbsp;B Preferred of a per share amount of at least $200.00, (iii) in the event that the closing market price of the Common Stock averages at least $7.50 per share over a period of 20 consecutive trading days and the daily trading volume averages at least 75,000 shares over such period, (iv) upon the approval of a majority of the then-outstanding shares of Series&nbsp;B, or (v) unless the Company is otherwise obligated to redeem the shares as described above, on April&nbsp;28, 2010.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">Each holder has the right to convert its shares of Series&nbsp;B into shares of Common Stock at the stated conversion rate at any time (subject to certain restrictions in the event such conversion would result in the holder being the beneficial holder of more than 4.99% of the Company&#146;s outstanding shares of common stock).</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The Warrants are exercisable for a period of five years commencing as of their issuance date, at an exercise price of $2.75 per share. The fair value of the warrants was $7,225,630. The value of the warrants was estimated using the Black-Scholes option pricing model with the following assumptions: average risk-free interest of 5.42%; dividend yield of 0%; average volatility factor of the expected market price of the Company&#146;s common stock of 70%; and a term of 3 years. In accordance with APB Opinion 14, the fair value of the warrants issued to the </P>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">In connection with the issuance of the Series&nbsp;B and related warrants, the Company entered into registration rights agreements granting the holders of the Series&nbsp;B certain demand and piggyback registration rights with respect to the common stock issuable upon conversion of the Series&nbsp;B and exercise of the warrants. The Company filed a registration statement with the SEC to register these shares for resale. The registration statement was declared effective December&nbsp;5, 2006. The registration rights agreement stipulated that if the registration statement was not declared effective by November&nbsp;21, 2006, the Company had to pay 1&nbsp;percent per month for a maximum of 6 months or 6&nbsp;percent maximum. Per paragraph 16 of EITF 00-19, this was determined to be an economic settlement alternative. Therefore, the warrants have been classified as equity. Between November&nbsp;21, 2006 and December&nbsp;4, 2006, the Company beca
me obligated to pay the Series&nbsp;B Preferred Shareholders approximately $134,000 in liquidated damages paid in the form of additional shares of Series&nbsp;B Preferred.</P>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The Company used three placement agents in connection with the offerings of the Series&nbsp;B. <P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">Chadbourn Securities, Inc. served as one of three of the Company&#146;s placement agents in connection with the offering, and for serving as such, received a cash fee from the Company of $446,050, and was issued warrants to acquire up to 210,980 shares of Common Stock at an exercise price of $2.75 per share and otherwise on the same terms as the warrants sold to the investors. These placement fees are included in the fees discussed in the paragraph above. Laird Cagan, a Managing Director of CMCP, acted as a registered representative of Chadbourn in connection with this offering. Our chief executive officer also works with CMCP.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">The fair value of the placement warrants was $2,224,903. The value of the warrants was estimated using the Black-Scholes option pricing model with the following assumptions: average risk-free interest of 5.42%; dividend yield of 0%; average volatility factor of the expected market price of the Company&#146;s common stock of 70%; and a term of 4 years. The value of the warrants was deducted along with the cash placement fees paid and expenses, $2,359,035, from the face value of the Series&nbsp;B, and is being amortized over 47 months. The amortization amount is treated consistent with the treatment of preferred stock dividends.</P>

<P style="line-height:13.25pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.667px"><B>NOTE 8. </B></P>
<P style="line-height:11.25pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:73.333px"><B>SHAREHOLDERS&#146; EQUITY</B></P>
<P style="line-height:11.25pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">Prior to the merger with Waste Solutions, Inc (WSI), WSI received $750,000 for the issuance of a promissory note and obtained a commitment for an additional $250,000 from an investor. The investor also received a warrant for the purchase of 133,333 shares of common stock for $0.01 per share in connection with these additional funds. These warrants were exercised in March&nbsp;of 2004. After the merger, the promissory note was exchanged for 500,000 shares of common stock in World Waste Technologies, Inc. In April&nbsp;2004, the Company received the additional $250,000 for the purchase of an additional 166,667 shares of common stock. The relative fair value allocated to the warrant was $170,844 using the Black-Scholes calculation. The value of the warrant was estimated using the Black Scholes option pricing model with the following assumptions:</P>
<P style="line-height:13.25pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.667px; padding-left:80px; text-indent:-32px; font-family:Symbol">&#183;</P>
<P style="line-height:11.25pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; padding-left:80px">average risk free interest of 3.6%; dividend yield of 0%; </P>
<P style="line-height:13.25pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.667px; padding-left:80px; text-indent:-32px; font-family:Symbol">&#183;</P>
<P style="line-height:11.25pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; padding-left:80px">average volatility factor of the expected market price of the Company&#146;s common stock of 70%; and</P>
<P style="line-height:13.25pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.667px; padding-left:80px; text-indent:-32px; font-family:Symbol">&#183;</P>
<P style="line-height:11.25pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; padding-left:80px">a term of 4 years.</P>
<P style="line-height:11.25pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">Prior to the merger of the Company with Voice Powered Technologies, Inc (VPTI), 500,000 shares of common stock were contributed to the Company by the founder of VPTI in connection with an agreement in which the founder sold approximately 1,000,000 other shares of common stock to accredited investors in a private sale.</P>
<P style="line-height:11.25pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:6.667px; text-indent:48px">During the second and third quarters ended June&nbsp;30, 2004 and September&nbsp;30, 2004 respectively, the Company obtained through a private placement an additional $3,093,910 from the sale of 2,311,872 shares of common stock, net of fees paid of $273,890 (2,245,206 of these shares were issued prior to the merger with VPTI on August&nbsp;24, 2004). Under a Registration Rights Agreement, the Company agreed to use commercially reasonable efforts to prepare and file a registration statement to register the resale of such shares within ninety days of completion of the Merger, August&nbsp;23, 2004, and use commercially reasonable efforts to cause such registration statement to be declared effective by the SEC as soon as practicable. The registration statement was declared effective December&nbsp;5, 2007.</P>
<P style="line-height:11.25pt; margin:0px; text-indent:48px">During July&nbsp;2004, the Company issued a warrant to a consultant for the purchase of 50,000 shares of common stock at an exercise price of $0.01 per share in consideration for investment banking, financial structuring and advisory services provided. The fair value of the warrant was $74,567. The value of the warrant was estimated using the Black-Scholes option pricing model with the following assumptions: average risk-free interest of 3.6%; dividend yield of 0%; average volatility factor of the expected market price of the Company&#146;s common stock of 26.4%; and a term of 4 years. The fair value of the warrant was expensed during the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2004. The warrant was exercised in full in September&nbsp;2004.</P>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>NOTE 8. </B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:96px"><B>SHAREHOLDERS&#146; EQUITY (CONTINUED)</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">Effective August&nbsp;24, 2004, World Waste Technologies, Inc. was merged into VPTI. Prior to the merger with VPTI, the holders of the convertible promissory notes converted these notes into 1,193,500 shares of common stock of World Waste Technologies, Inc.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">Subsequent to the merger with VPTI, during the third and fourth quarters of the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2004, in connection with a private placement of securities, the Company sold 1,192,000 units; each unit comprised of one (1) share of common stock in the Company and warrants exercisable for 0.25 shares (298,000 shares) of common stock of the Company at an exercise price of $0.01 per share for 5 years. The fair value of the warrants was $742,222. The value of the warrants was estimated using the Black-Scholes option pricing model with the following assumptions: average risk-free interest of 3.6%; dividend yield of 0%; average volatility factor of the expected market price of the Company&#146;s common stock of 70%; and a term of 1 to 4 years. The consideration paid for the units was $2.50 per unit, for aggregate net proceeds to the Company of $1,879,770. As of December&nbsp;31, 2004, 152,000 of these warrants had been exercised for net 
proceeds to the Company of $1,520. Under the Registration Rights Agreement, the Company agreed to use commercially reasonable efforts to prepare and file a registration statement within ninety days of completion of the private placement and use commercially reasonable efforts to cause such registration statement to be declared effective by the SEC as soon as practicable registering the resale of the shares and shares underlying the warrants. The registration statement was declared effective December&nbsp;5, 2007.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">During the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2006, in connection with private placements of unregistered securities, the Company raised gross proceeds of $3,387,000 by issuing 1,354,800 units (each unit comprised of one (1) share of common stock in the Company (1,354,800 shares of common stock) and warrants exercisable for 0.25 shares (338,700 warrants)) at a purchase price of $2.50 per unit. The warrants expire five years after the date of the sale of the shares and are exercisable at $0.01 per share, subject to adjustment. All of the warrants were exercised during the quarter ended March&nbsp;31, 2006. The fair value of the warrants was $843,487. The value of the warrants was estimated using the Black-Scholes option pricing model with the following assumptions: average risk-free interest of 3.75%; dividend yield of 0%; average volatility factor of the expected market price of the Company&#146;s common stock of 70%; and a term of one year. Under t
he Registration Rights Agreement, the Company agreed to use commercially reasonable efforts to prepare and file a registration statement within ninety days of completion of the private placement and use commercially reasonable efforts to cause such registration statement to be declared effective by the SEC as soon as practicable registering the resale of shares and the shares underlying the warrants. The registration statement was declared effective December&nbsp;5, 2006.</P>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>NOTE 11. </B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:73.333px"><B>RELATED PARTY TRANSACTIONS</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">During 2006, Chadbourn Securities Inc. (&#147;Chadbourn&#148;) &nbsp;acted as the placement agent for the Company in connection with the private placement of 1,354,800 shares of the Company&#146;s common stock and warrants to purchase 338,700 shares of the Company&#146;s common stock, the private placement of 4,075,600 shares of the Company&#146;s Series&nbsp;A Preferred Stock and warrants to purchase 407,560 shares of the Company&#146;s common stock, and $4,015,000 aggregate principal amount of the Company&#146;s senior secured promissory notes and warrants to purchase up to a total of 529,980 shares of Common Stock. In connection with those private placements, the Company paid the Placement Agent a commission of approximately $961,550. In addition, the Company paid the Placement Agent a non-accountable expense allowance of $267,740 and issued the Placement Agent, or its affiliates, warrants to purchase 548,486 of the Company&#146;s common s
hares, at exercise price of $2.50. The values of the warrants, $756,247, were estimated using the Black-Scholes option pricing model with the following assumptions: average risk-free interest rate 3.6% to 6.75%; dividend yield of 0%; average volatility factor of the expected market price of the Company&#146;s common stock of 70%; and a term of 4 years.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">During the quarter ended March&nbsp;31, 2007, the Placement Agent acted as the placement agent for the Company in connection with the private placement of the Company&#146;s senior secured promissory notes and warrants to purchase up to a total of 297,000 shares of Common Stock. In connection with this private placement, the Company paid the Placement Agent a commission of $27,500.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:48px">Chadbourn served as one of three of the Company&#146;s placement agents in connection with the offering of the Company&#146;s Series&nbsp;B Preferred Stock, and for serving as such, received a cash fee from the Company of $446,050, and was issued warrants to acquire up to 210,980 shares of Common Stock at an exercise price of $2.75 per share and otherwise on the same terms as the Warrants sold to the investors.</P>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px"><B>NOTE 13. </B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:8.867px; text-indent:73.333px"><B>SUBSEQUENT EVENTS</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:13.333px; text-indent:48px">On February 2, 2009, the Company loaned Vertex Energy, LP $1.0 million. &nbsp;The note accrues interest at 12% per annum and is due at the earliest of: the consummation of the close of the merger with the Company, April 30, 2009, or 60 days following the termination of the merger. &nbsp;Upon an event of default, interest accrues at 15%. &nbsp;The proceeds were used by Vertex Energy, LP for working capital purposes. &nbsp;The note is secured by the assets of Vertex Energy, LP and is junior to existing bank debt.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:13.333px; text-indent:48px">At a special meeting of its shareholders held on March 6, 2009, the holders of a majority of the outstanding shares of each of World Waste&#146;s common stock, Series A preferred stock and Series B preferred stock, adopted the merger agreement among the Company, Vertex Energy, LP, a Texas limited partnership, Vertex Nevada, Vertex Merger Sub, LLC, a California limited liability company and wholly owned subsidiary of Vertex Nevada, and Benjamin P. Cowart, as agent for the shareholders of Vertex Nevada. &nbsp;Upon consummation of the merger, the Company will become a wholly owned subsidiary of Vertex Nevada, and Vertex Nevada will succeed to the &nbsp;Company&#146;s reporting obligations under the Securities Exchange Act of 1934. &nbsp;Although the parties believe that all of the conditions to the closing of the merger have been met, the parties anticipate that the merger will not be consummated until the close of business on April 1, 2009. </
P>
